10084{_}2517{_}But the big husky turned away sullenly, growling, still snarling, and vented his rage by nipping fiercely at the flank of one of his sledge-mates.
10084{_}2518{_}Gray Wolf understood what had happened, though she could not see.
10084{_}2519{_}She shrank closer to Kazan.
10084{_}2520{_}She knew that the moon and the stars had looked down on that thing that always meant death--the challenge to the right of mate.
10084{_}2521{_}With her luring coyness, whining and softly muzzling his shoulder and neck, she tried to draw Kazan away from the pad-beaten circle in which the bull lay.
10084{_}2522{_}Kazan's answer was an ominous rolling of smothered thunder deep down in his throat.
10084{_}2523{_}He lay down beside her, licked her blind face swiftly, and faced the stranger dogs.
10084{_}2524{_}The moon sank lower and lower and at last dropped behind the western forests.
10084{_}2525{_}The stars grew paler.
10084{_}2526{_}One by one they faded from the sky and after a time there followed the cold gray dawn of the North.
10084{_}2527{_}In that dawn the big husky leader rose from the hole he had made in the snow and returned to the bull.
10084{_}2528{_}Kazan, alert, was on his feet in an instant and stood also close to the bull.
10084{_}2529{_}The two circled ominously, their heads lowered, their crests bristling.
10084{_}2530{_}The husky drew away, and Kazan crouched at the bull's neck and began tearing at the frozen flesh.
10084{_}2531{_}He was not hungry.
10084{_}2532{_}But in this way he showed his right to the flesh, his defiance of the right of the big husky.
10084{_}2533{_}For a few seconds he forgot Gray Wolf.
10084{_}2534{_}The husky had slipped back like a shadow and now he stood again over Gray Wolf, sniffing her neck and body.
10084{_}2535{_}Then he whined.
10084{_}2536{_}In that whine were the passion, the invitation, the demand of the Wild.
10084{_}2537{_}So quickly that the eye could scarcely follow her movement faithful Gray Wolf sank her gleaming fangs in the husky's shoulder.
10084{_}2538{_}A gray streak--nothing more tangible than a streak of gray, silent and terrible, shot through the dawn-gloom.
10084{_}2539{_}It was Kazan.
10084{_}2540{_}He came without a snarl, without a cry, and in a moment he and the husky were in the throes of terrific battle.
10084{_}2541{_}The four other huskies ran in quickly and stood waiting a dozen paces from the combatants.
10084{_}2542{_}Gray Wolf lay crouched on her belly.
10084{_}2543{_}The giant husky and the quarter-strain wolf-dog were not fighting like sledge-dog or wolf.
10084{_}2544{_}For a few moments rage and hatred made them fight like mongrels.
10084{_}2545{_}Both had holds.
10084{_}2546{_}Now one was down, and now the other, and so swiftly did they change their positions that the four waiting sledge-dogs were puzzled and stood motionless.
10084{_}2547{_}Under other conditions they would have leaped upon the first of the fighters to be thrown upon his back and torn him to pieces.
10084{_}2548{_}That was the way of the wolf and the wolf-dog.
10084{_}2549{_}But now they stood back, hesitating and fearful.
10084{_}2550{_}The big husky had never been beaten in battle.
10084{_}2551{_}Great Dane ancestors had given him a huge bulk and a jaw that could crush an ordinary dog's head.
10084{_}2552{_}But in Kazan he was meeting not only the dog and the wolf, but all that was best in the two.
10084{_}2553{_}And Kazan had the advantage of a few hours of rest and a full stomach.
10084{_}2554{_}More than that, he was fighting for Gray Wolf.
10084{_}2555{_}His fangs had sunk deep in the husky's shoulder, and the husky's long teeth met through the hide and flesh of his neck.
10084{_}2556{_}An inch deeper, and they would have pierced his jugular.
10084{_}2557{_}Kazan knew this, as he crunched his enemy's shoulder-bone, and every instant--even in their fiercest struggling--he was guarding against a second and more successful lunge of those powerful jaws.
10084{_}2558{_}At last the lunge came, and quicker than the wolf itself Kazan freed himself and leaped back.
10084{_}2559{_}His chest dripped blood, but he did not feel the hurt.
10084{_}2560{_}They began slowly to circle, and now the watching sledge-dogs drew a step or two nearer, and their jaws drooled nervously and their red eyes glared as they waited for the fatal moment.
10084{_}2561{_}Their eyes were on the big husky.
10084{_}2562{_}He became the pivot of Kazan's wider circle now, and he limped as he turned.
10084{_}2563{_}His shoulder was broken.
10084{_}2564{_}His ears were flattened as he watched Kazan.
10084{_}2565{_}Kazan's ears were erect, and his feet touched the snow lightly.
10084{_}2566{_}All his fighting cleverness and all his caution had returned to him.
10084{_}2567{_}The blind rage of a few moments was gone and he fought now as he had fought his deadliest enemy, the long-clawed lynx.
10084{_}2568{_}Five times he circled around the husky, and then like a shot he was in, sending his whole weight against the husky's shoulder, with the momentum of a ten-foot leap behind it.
10084{_}2569{_}This time he did not try for a hold, but slashed at the husky's jaws.
10084{_}2570{_}It was the deadliest of all attacks when that merciless tribunal of death stood waiting for the first fall of the vanquished.
10084{_}2571{_}The huge dog was thrown from his feet.
10084{_}2572{_}For a fatal moment he rolled upon his side and in the moment his four sledge-mates were upon him.
10084{_}2573{_}All of their hatred of the weeks and months in which the long-fanged leader had bullied them in the traces was concentrated upon him now and he was literally torn into pieces.
10084{_}2574{_}Kazan pranced to Gray Wolf's side and with a joyful whine she laid her head over his neck.
10084{_}2575{_}Twice he had fought the Fight of Death for her.
10084{_}2576{_}Twice he had won.
10084{_}2577{_}And in her blindness Gray Wolf's soul--if soul she had--rose in exultation to the cold gray sky, and her breast panted against Kazan's shoulder as she listened to the crunching of fangs in the flesh and bone of the foe her lord and master had overthrown.
10084{_}2578{_}CHAPTER XVI  THE CALL   Followed days of feasting on the frozen flesh of the old bull.
10084{_}2579{_}In vain Gray Wolf tried to lure Kazan off into the forests and the swamps.
10084{_}2580{_}Day by day the temperature rose.
10084{_}2581{_}There was hunting now.
10084{_}2582{_}And Gray Wolf wanted to be alone--with Kazan.
10084{_}2583{_}But with Kazan, as with most men, leadership and power roused new sensations.
10084{_}2584{_}And he was the leader of the dog-pack, as he had once been a leader among the wolves.
10084{_}2585{_}Not only Gray Wolf followed at his flank now, but the four huskies trailed behind him.
10084{_}2586{_}Once more he was experiencing that triumph and strange thrill that he had almost forgotten and only Gray Wolf, in that eternal night of her blindness, felt with dread foreboding the danger into which his newly achieved czarship might lead him.
10084{_}2587{_}For three days and three nights they remained in the neighborhood of the dead moose, ready to defend it against others, and yet each day and each night growing less vigilant in their guard.
10084{_}2588{_}Then came the fourth night, on which they killed a young doe.
10084{_}2589{_}Kazan led in that chase and for the first time, in the excitement of having the pack at his back, he left his blind mate behind.
10084{_}2590{_}When they came to the kill he was the first to leap at its soft throat.
10084{_}2591{_}And not until he had begun to tear at the doe's flesh did the others dare to eat.
10084{_}2592{_}He was master.
10084{_}2593{_}He could send them back with a snarl.
10084{_}2594{_}At the gleam of his fangs they crouched quivering on their bellies in the snow.
10084{_}2595{_}Kazan's blood was fomented with brute exultation, and the excitement and fascination that came in the possession of new power took the place of Gray Wolf each day a little more.
10084{_}2596{_}She came in half an hour after the kill, and there was no longer the lithesome alertness to her slender legs, or gladness in the tilt of her ears or the poise of her head.
10084{_}2597{_}She did not eat much of the doe.
10084{_}2598{_}Her blind face was turned always in Kazan's direction.
10084{_}2599{_}Wherever he moved she followed with her unseeing eyes, as if expecting each moment his old signal to her--that low throat-note that had called to her so often when they were alone in the wilderness.
10084{_}2600{_}In Kazan, as leader of the pack, there was working a curious change.
10084{_}2601{_}If his mates had been wolves it would not have been difficult for Gray Wolf to have lured him away.
10084{_}2602{_}But Kazan was among his own kind.
10084{_}2603{_}He was a dog.
10084{_}2604{_}And they were dogs.
10084{_}2605{_}Fires that had burned down and ceased to warm him flamed up in him anew.
10084{_}2606{_}In his life with Gray Wolf one thing had oppressed him as it could not oppress her, and that thing was loneliness.
10084{_}2607{_}Nature had created him of that kind which requires companionship--not of one but of many.
10084{_}2608{_}It had given him birth that he might listen to and obey the commands of the voice of man.
10084{_}2609{_}He had grown to hate men, but of the dogs--his kind--he was a part.
10084{_}2610{_}He had been happy with Gray Wolf, happier than he had ever been in the companionship of men and his blood-brothers.
10084{_}2611{_}But he had been a long time separated from the life that had once been his and the call of blood made him for a time forget.
10084{_}2612{_}And only Gray Wolf, with that wonderful super-instinct which nature was giving her in place of her lost sight, foresaw the end to which it was leading him.
10084{_}2613{_}Each day the temperature continued to rise until when the sun was warmest the snow began to thaw a little.
10084{_}2614{_}This was two weeks after the fight near the bull.
10084{_}2615{_}Gradually the pack had swung eastward, until it was now fifty miles east and twenty miles south of the old home under the windfall.
10084{_}2616{_}More than ever Gray Wolf began to long for their old nest under the fallen trees.
10084{_}2617{_}Again with those first promises of spring in sunshine and air, there was coming also for the second time in her life the promise of approaching motherhood.
10084{_}2618{_}But her efforts to draw Kazan back were unavailing, and in spite of her protest he wandered each day a little farther east and south at the head of his pack.
10084{_}2619{_}Instinct impelled the four huskies to move in that direction.
10084{_}2620{_}They had not yet been long enough a part of the wild to forget the necessity of man and in that direction there was man.
10084{_}2621{_}In that direction, and not far from them now, was the Hudson Bay Company's post to which they and their dead master owed their allegiance.
10084{_}2622{_}Kazan did not know this, but one day something happened to bring back visions and desires that widened still more the gulf between him and Gray Wolf.
10084{_}2623{_}They had come to the cap of a ridge when something stopped them.
10084{_}2624{_}It was a man's voice crying shrilly that word of long ago that had so often stirred the blood in Kazan's own veins--"_m'hoosh!
10084{_}2625{_}m'hoosh!
10084{_}2626{_}m'hoosh!
10084{_}2627{_}"_--and from the ridge they looked down upon the open space of the plain, where a team of six dogs was trotting ahead of a sledge, with a man running behind them, urging them on at every other step with that cry of "_m'hoosh!
10084{_}2628{_}m'hoosh!
10084{_}2629{_}m'hoosh!
10084{_}2630{_}"_  Trembling and undecided, the four huskies and the wolf-dog stood on the ridge with Gray Wolf cringing behind them.
10084{_}2631{_}Not until man and dogs and sledge had disappeared did they move, and then they trotted down to the trail and sniffed at it whiningly and excitedly.
10084{_}2632{_}For a mile or two they followed it, Kazan and his mates going fearlessly in the trail.
10084{_}2633{_}Gray Wolf hung back, traveling twenty yards to the right of them, with the hot man-scent driving the blood feverishly through her brain.
10084{_}2634{_}Only her love for Kazan--and the faith she still had in him--kept her that near.
10084{_}2635{_}At the edge of a swamp Kazan halted and turned away from the trail.
10084{_}2636{_}With the desire that was growing in him there was still that old suspicion which nothing could quite wipe out--the suspicion that was an inheritance of his quarter-strain of wolf.
10084{_}2637{_}Gray Wolf whined joyfully when he turned into the forest, and drew so close to him that her shoulder rubbed against Kazan's as they traveled side by side.
10084{_}2638{_}The "slush" snows followed fast after this.
10084{_}2639{_}And the "slush" snows meant spring--and the emptying of the wilderness of human life.
10084{_}2640{_}Kazan and his mates soon began to scent the presence and the movement of this life.
10084{_}2641{_}They were now within thirty miles of the post.
10084{_}2642{_}For a hundred miles on all sides of them the trappers were moving in with their late winter's catch of furs.
10084{_}2643{_}From east and west, south and north, all trails led to the post.
10084{_}2644{_}The pack was caught in the mesh of them.
10084{_}2645{_}For a week not a day passed that they did not cross a fresh trail, and sometimes two or three.
10084{_}2646{_}Gray Wolf was haunted by constant fear.
10084{_}2647{_}In her blindness she knew that they were surrounded by the menace of men.
10084{_}2648{_}To Kazan what was coming to pass had more and more ceased to fill him with fear and caution.
10084{_}2649{_}Three times that week he heard the shouts of men--and once he heard a white man's laughter and the barking of dogs as their master tossed them their daily feed of fish.
10084{_}2650{_}In the air he caught the pungent scent of camp-fires and one night, in the far distance, he heard a wild snatch of song, followed by the yelping and barking of a dog-pack.
10084{_}2651{_}Slowly and surely the lure of man drew him nearer to the post--a mile to-night, two miles to-morrow, but always nearer.
10084{_}2652{_}And Gray Wolf, fighting her losing fight to the end, sensed in the danger-filled air the nearness of that hour when he would respond to the final call and she would be left alone.
10084{_}2653{_}These were days of activity and excitement at the fur company's post, the days of accounting, of profit and of pleasure;--the days when the wilderness poured in its treasure of fur, to be sent a little later to London and Paris and the capitals of Europe.
10084{_}2654{_}And this year there was more than the usual interest in the foregathering of the forest people.
10084{_}2655{_}The plague had wrought its terrible havoc, and not until the fur-hunters had come to answer to the spring roll-call would it be known accurately who had lived and who had died.
10084{_}2656{_}The Chippewans and half-breeds from the south began to arrive first, with their teams of mongrel curs, picked up along the borders of civilization.
10084{_}2657{_}Close after them came the hunters from the western barren lands, bringing with them loads of white fox and caribou skins, and an army of big-footed, long-legged Mackenzie hounds that pulled like horses and wailed like whipped puppies when the huskies and Eskimo dogs set upon them.
10084{_}2658{_}Packs of fierce Labrador dogs, never vanquished except by death, came from close to Hudson's Bay.
10084{_}2659{_}Team after team of little yellow and gray Eskimo dogs, as quick with their fangs as were their black and swift-running masters with their hands and feet, met the much larger and dark-colored Malemutes from the Athabasca.
10084{_}2660{_}Enemies of all these packs of fierce huskies trailed in from all sides, fighting, snapping and snarling, with the lust of killing deep born in them from their wolf progenitors.
10084{_}2661{_}There was no cessation in the battle of the fangs.
10084{_}2662{_}It began with the first brute arrivals.
10084{_}2663{_}It continued from dawn through the day and around the camp-fires at night.
10084{_}2664{_}There was never an end to the strife between the dogs, and between the men and the dogs.
10084{_}2665{_}The snow was trailed and stained with blood and the scent of it added greater fierceness to the wolf-breeds.
10084{_}2666{_}Half a dozen battles were fought to the death each day and night.
10084{_}2667{_}Those that died were chiefly the south-bred curs--mixtures of mastiff, Great Dane, and sheep-dog--and the fatally slow Mackenzie hounds.
10084{_}2668{_}About the post rose the smoke of a hundred camp-fires, and about these fires gathered the women and the children of the hunters.
10084{_}2669{_}When the snow was no longer fit for sledging, Williams, the factor, noted that there were many who had not come, and the accounts of these he later scratched out of his ledgers knowing that they were victims of the plague.
10084{_}2670{_}At last came the night of the Big Carnival, For weeks and months women and children and men had been looking forward to this.
10084{_}2671{_}In scores of forest cabins, in smoke-blackened tepees, and even in the frozen homes of the little Eskimos, anticipation of this wild night of pleasure had given an added zest to life.
10084{_}2672{_}It was the Big Circus--the good time given twice each year by the company to its people.
10084{_}2673{_}This year, to offset the memory of plague and death, the factor had put forth unusual exertions.
10084{_}2674{_}His hunters had killed four fat caribou.
10084{_}2675{_}In the clearing there were great piles of dry logs, and in the center of all there rose eight ten-foot tree-butts crotched at the top; and from crotch to crotch there rested a stout sapling stripped of bark, and on each sapling was spitted the carcass of a caribou, to be roasted whole by the heat of the fire beneath.
10084{_}2676{_}The fires were lighted at dusk, and Williams himself started the first of those wild songs of the Northland--the song of the caribou, as the flames leaped up into the dark night.
10084{_}2677{_}"Oh, ze cariboo-oo-oo, ze cariboo-oo-oo,     He roas' on high,     Jes' under ze sky.
10084{_}2678{_}air-holes beeg white cariboo-oo-oo!"
10084{_}2679{_}"Now!"
10084{_}2680{_}he yelled.
10084{_}2681{_}"Now--all together!"
10084{_}2682{_}And carried away by his enthusiasm, the forest people awakened from their silence of months, and the song burst forth in a savage frenzy that reached to the skies.
10084{_}2683{_}*       *       *       *       *  Two miles to the south and west that first thunder of human voice reached the ears of Kazan and Gray Wolf and the masterless huskies.
10084{_}2684{_}And with the voices of men they heard now the excited howlings of dogs.
10084{_}2685{_}The huskies faced the direction of the sounds, moving restlessly and whining.
10084{_}2686{_}For a few moments Kazan stood as though carven of rock.
10084{_}2687{_}Then he turned his head, and his first look was to Gray Wolf.
10084{_}2688{_}She had slunk back a dozen feet and lay crouched under the thick cover of a balsam shrub.
10084{_}2689{_}Her body, legs and neck were flattened in the snow.
10084{_}2690{_}She made no sound, but her lips were drawn back and her teeth shone white.
10084{_}2691{_}Kazan trotted back to her, sniffed at her blind face and whined.
10084{_}2692{_}Gray Wolf still did not move.
10084{_}2693{_}He returned to the dogs and his jaws opened and closed with a snap.
10084{_}2694{_}Still more clearly came the wild voice of the carnival, and no longer to be held back by Kazan's leadership, the four huskies dropped their heads and slunk like shadows in its direction.
10084{_}2695{_}Kazan hesitated, urging Gray Wolf.
10084{_}2696{_}But not a muscle of Gray Wolf's body moved.
10084{_}2697{_}She would have followed him in face of fire but not in face of man.
10084{_}2698{_}Not a sound escaped her ears.
10084{_}2699{_}She heard the quick fall of Kazan's feet as he left her.
10084{_}2700{_}In another moment she knew that he was gone.
10084{_}2701{_}Then--and not until then--did she lift her head, and from her soft throat there broke a whimpering cry.
10084{_}2702{_}It was her last call to Kazan.
10084{_}2703{_}But stronger than that there was running through Kazan's excited blood the call of man and of dog.
10084{_}2704{_}The huskies were far in advance of him now and for a few moments he raced madly to overtake them.
10084{_}2705{_}Then he slowed down until he was trotting, and a hundred yards farther on he stopped.
10084{_}2706{_}Less than a mile away he could see where the flames of the great fires were reddening the sky.
10084{_}2707{_}He gazed back to see if Gray Wolf was following and then went on until he struck an open and hard traveled trail.
10084{_}2708{_}It was beaten with the footprints of men and dogs, and over it two of the caribou had been dragged a day or two before.
10084{_}2709{_}At last he came to the thinned out strip of timber that surrounded the clearing and the flare of the flames was in his eyes.
10084{_}2710{_}The bedlam of sound that came to him now was like fire in his brain.
10084{_}2711{_}He heard the song and the laughter of men, the shrill cries of women and children, the barking and snarling and fighting of a hundred dogs.
10084{_}2712{_}He wanted to rush out and join them, to become again a part of what he had once been.
10084{_}2713{_}Yard by yard he sneaked through the thin timber until he reached the edge of the clearing.
10084{_}2714{_}There he stood in the shadow of a spruce and looked out upon life as he had once lived it, trembling, wistful and yet hesitating in that final moment.
10084{_}2715{_}A hundred yards away was the savage circle of men and dogs and fire.
10084{_}2716{_}His nostrils were filled with the rich aroma of the roasting caribou, and as he crouched down, still with that wolfish caution that Gray Wolf had taught him, men with long poles brought the huge carcasses crashing down upon the melting snow about the fires.
10084{_}2717{_}In one great rush the horde of wild revelers crowded in with bared knives, and a snarling mass of dogs closed in behind them.
10084{_}2718{_}In another moment he had forgotten Gray Wolf, had forgotten all that man and the wild had taught him, and like a gray streak was across the open.
10084{_}2719{_}The dogs were surging back when he reached them, with half a dozen of the factor's men lashing them in the faces with long caribou-gut whips.
10084{_}2720{_}The sting of a lash fell in a fierce cut over an Eskimo dog's shoulder, and in snapping at the lash his fangs struck Kazan's rump.
10084{_}2721{_}With lightning swiftness Kazan returned the cut, and in an instant the jaws of the dogs had met.
10084{_}2722{_}In another instant they were down and Kazan had the Eskimo dog by the throat.
10084{_}2723{_}With shouts the men rushed in.
10084{_}2724{_}Again and again their whips cut like knives through the air.
10084{_}2725{_}Their blows fell on Kazan, who was uppermost, and as he felt the burning pain of the scourging whips there flooded through him all at once the fierce memory of the days of old--the days of the Club and the Lash.
10084{_}2726{_}He snarled.
10084{_}2727{_}Slowly he loosened his hold of the Eskimo dog's throat.
10084{_}2728{_}And then, out of the melee of dogs and men, there sprang another man--_with a club_!
10084{_}2729{_}It fell on Kazan's back and the force of it sent him flat into the snow.
10084{_}2730{_}It was raised again.
10084{_}2731{_}Behind the club there was a face--a brutal, fire-reddened face.
10084{_}2732{_}It was such a face that had driven Kazan into the wild, and as the club fell again he evaded the full weight of its blow and his fangs gleamed like ivory knives.
10084{_}2733{_}A third time the club was raised, and this time Kazan met it in mid-air, and his teeth ripped the length of the man's forearm.
10084{_}2734{_}"Good God!"
10084{_}2735{_}shrieked the man in pain, and Kazan caught the gleam of a rifle barrel as he sped toward the forest.
10084{_}2736{_}A shot followed.
10084{_}2737{_}Something like a red-hot coal ran the length of Kazan's hip, and deep in the forest he stopped to lick at the burning furrow where the bullet had gone just deep enough to take the skin and hair from his flesh.
10084{_}2738{_}*       *       *       *       *  Gray Wolf was still waiting under the balsam shrub when Kazan returned to her.
10084{_}2739{_}Joyously she sprang forth to meet him.
10084{_}2740{_}Once more the man had sent back the old Kazan to her.
10084{_}2741{_}He muzzled her neck and face, and stood for a few moments with his head resting across her back, listening to the distant sound.
10084{_}2742{_}Then, with ears laid flat, he set out straight into the north and west.
10084{_}2743{_}And now Gray Wolf ran shoulder to shoulder with him like the Gray Wolf of the days before the dog-pack came; for that wonderful thing that lay beyond the realm of reason told her that once more she was comrade and mate, and that their trail that night was leading to their old home under the windfall.
10084{_}2744{_}CHAPTER XVII  HIS SON   It happened that Kazan was to remember three things above all others.
10084{_}2745{_}He could never quite forget his old days in the traces, though they were growing more shadowy and indistinct in his memory as the summers and the winters passed.
10084{_}2746{_}Like a dream there came to him a memory of the time he had gone down to Civilization.
10084{_}2747{_}Like dreams were the visions that rose before him now and then of the face of the First Woman, and of the faces of masters who--to him--had lived ages ago.
10084{_}2748{_}And never would he quite forget the Fire, and his fights with man and beast, and his long chases in the moonlight.
10084{_}2749{_}But two things were always with him as if they had been but yesterday, rising clear and unforgetable above all others, like the two stars in the North that never lost their brilliance.
10084{_}2750{_}One was Woman.
10084{_}2751{_}The other was the terrible fight of that night on the top of the Sun Rock, when the lynx had blinded forever his wild mate, Gray Wolf.
10084{_}2752{_}Certain events remain indelibly fixed in the minds of men; and so, in a not very different way, they remain in the minds of beasts.
10084{_}2753{_}It takes neither brain nor reason to measure the depths of sorrow or of happiness.
10084{_}2754{_}And Kazan in his unreasoning way knew that contentment and peace, a full stomach, and caresses and kind words instead of blows had come to him through Woman, and that comradeship in the wilderness--faith, loyalty and devotion--were a part of Gray Wolf.
10084{_}2755{_}The third unforgetable thing was about to occur in the home they had found for themselves under the swamp windfall during the days of cold and famine.
10084{_}2756{_}They had left the swamp over a month before when it was smothered deep in snow.
10084{_}2757{_}On the day they returned to it the sun was shining warmly in the first glorious days of spring warmth.
10084{_}2758{_}Everywhere, big and small, there were the rushing torrents of melting snows and the crackle of crumbling ice, the dying cries of thawing rock and earth and tree, and each night for many nights past the cold pale glow of the aurora borealis had crept farther and farther toward the Pole in fading glory.
10084{_}2759{_}So early as this the poplar buds had begun to swell and the air was filled with the sweet odor of balsam, spruce and cedar.
10084{_}2760{_}Where there had been famine and death and stillness six weeks before, Kazan and Gray Wolf now stood at the edge of the swamp and breathed the earthy smells of spring, and listened to the sounds of life.
10084{_}2761{_}Over their heads a pair of newly-mated moose-birds fluttered and scolded at them.
10084{_}2762{_}A big jay sat pluming himself in the sunshine.
10084{_}2763{_}Farther in they heard the crack of a stick broken under a heavy hoof.
10084{_}2764{_}From the ridge behind them they caught the raw scent of a mother bear, busy pulling down the tender poplar buds for her six-weeks-old cubs, born while she was still deep in her winter sleep.
10084{_}2765{_}In the warmth of the sun and the sweetness of the air there breathed to Gray Wolf the mystery of matehood and of motherhood.
10084{_}2766{_}She whined softly and rubbed her blind face against Kazan.
10084{_}2767{_}For days, in her way, she tried to tell him.
10084{_}2768{_}More than ever she wanted to curl herself up in that warm dry nest under the windfall.
10084{_}2769{_}She had no desire to hunt.
10084{_}2770{_}The crack of the dry stick under a cloven hoof and the warm scent of the she-bear and her cubs roused none of the old instincts in her.
10084{_}2771{_}She wanted to curl herself up in the old windfall--and wait.
10084{_}2772{_}And she tried hard to make Kazan understand her desire.
10084{_}2773{_}Now that the snow was gone they found that a narrow creek lay between them and the knoll on which the windfall was situated.
10084{_}2774{_}Gray Wolf picked up her ears at the tumult of the little torrent.
10084{_}2775{_}Since the day of the Fire, when Kazan and she had saved themselves on the sand-bar, she had ceased to have the inherent wolf horror of water.
10084{_}2776{_}She followed fearlessly, even eagerly, behind Kazan as he sought a place where they could ford the rushing little stream.
10084{_}2777{_}On the other side Kazan could see the big windfall.
10084{_}2778{_}Gray Wolf could _smell_ it and she whined joyously, with her blind face turned toward it.
10084{_}2779{_}A hundred yards up the stream a big cedar had fallen over it and Kazan began to cross.
10084{_}2780{_}For a moment Gray Wolf hesitated, and then followed.
10084{_}2781{_}Side by side they trotted to the windfall.
10084{_}2782{_}With their heads and shoulders in the dark opening to their nest they scented the air long and cautiously.
10084{_}2783{_}Then they entered.
10084{_}2784{_}Kazan heard Gray Wolf as she flung herself down on the dry floor of the snug cavern.
10084{_}2785{_}She was panting, not from exhaustion, but because she was filled with a sensation of contentment and happiness.
10084{_}2786{_}In the darkness Kazan's own jaws fell apart.
10084{_}2787{_}He, too, was glad to get back to their old home.
10084{_}2788{_}He went to Gray Wolf and, panting still harder, she licked his face.
10084{_}2789{_}It had but one meaning.
10084{_}2790{_}And Kazan understood.
10084{_}2791{_}For a moment he lay down beside her, listening, and eyeing the opening to their nest.
10084{_}2792{_}Then he began to sniff about the log walls.
10084{_}2793{_}He was close to the opening when a sudden fresh scent came to him, and he grew rigid, and his bristles stood up.
10084{_}2794{_}The scent was followed by a whimpering, babyish chatter.
10084{_}2795{_}A porcupine entered the opening and proceeded to advance in its foolish fashion, still chattering in that babyish way that has made its life inviolable at the hands of man.
10084{_}2796{_}Kazan had heard that sound before, and like all other beasts had learned to ignore the presence of the innocuous creature that made it.
10084{_}2797{_}But just now he did not stop to consider that what he saw was a porcupine and that at his first snarl the good-humored little creature would waddle away as fast as it could, still chattering baby talk to itself.
10084{_}2798{_}His first reasoning was that it was a live thing invading the home to which Gray Wolf and he had just returned.
10084{_}2799{_}A day later, or perhaps an hour later, he would have driven it back with a growl.
10084{_}2800{_}Now he leaped upon it.
10084{_}2801{_}A wild chattering, intermingled with pig-like squeaks, and then a rising staccato of howls followed the attack.
10084{_}2802{_}Gray Wolf sprang to the opening.
10084{_}2803{_}The porcupine was rolled up in a thousand-spiked ball a dozen feet away, and she could hear Kazan tearing about in the throes of the direst agony that can befall a beast of the forests.
10084{_}2804{_}His face and nose were a mat of quills.
10084{_}2805{_}For a few moments he rolled and dug in the wet mold and earth, pawing madly at the things that pierced his flesh.
10084{_}2806{_}Then he set off like all dogs will who have come into contact with the friendly porcupine, and raced again and again around the windfall, howling at every jump.
10084{_}2807{_}Gray Wolf took the matter coolly.
10084{_}2808{_}It is possible that at times there are moments of humor in the lives of animals.
10084{_}2809{_}If so, she saw this one.
10084{_}2810{_}She scented the porcupine and she knew that Kazan was full of quills.
10084{_}2811{_}As there was nothing to do and nothing to fight she sat back on her haunches and waited, pricking up her ears every time Kazan passed her in his mad circuit around the windfall.
10084{_}2812{_}At his fourth or fifth heat the porcupine smoothed itself down a little, and continuing the interrupted thread of its chatter waddled to a near-by poplar, climbed it and began to gnaw the tender bark from a limb.
10084{_}2813{_}At last Kazan halted before Gray Wolf.
10084{_}2814{_}The first agony of a hundred little needles piercing his flesh had deadened into a steady burning pain.
10084{_}2815{_}Gray Wolf went over to him and investigated him cautiously.
10084{_}2816{_}With her teeth she seized the ends of two or three of the quills and pulled them out.
10084{_}2817{_}Kazan was very much dog now.
10084{_}2818{_}He gave a yelp, and whimpered as Gray Wolf jerked out a second bunch of quills.
10084{_}2819{_}Then he flattened himself on his belly, stretched out his forelegs, closed his eyes, and without any other sound except an occasional yelp of pain allowed Gray Wolf to go on with the operation.
10084{_}2820{_}Fortunately he had escaped getting any of the quills in his mouth and tongue.
10084{_}2821{_}But his nose and jaws were soon red with blood.
10084{_}2822{_}For an hour Gray Wolf kept faithfully at her task and by the end of that time had succeeded in pulling out most of the quills.
10084{_}2823{_}A few still remained, too short and too deeply inbedded for her to extract with her teeth.
10084{_}2824{_}After this Kazan went down to the creek and buried his burning muzzle in the cold water.
10084{_}2825{_}This gave him some relief, but only for a short time.
10084{_}2826{_}The quills that remained worked their way deeper and deeper into his flesh, like living things.
10084{_}2827{_}Nose and lips began to swell.
10084{_}2828{_}Blood and saliva dripped from his mouth and his eyes grew red.
10084{_}2829{_}Two hours after Gray Wolf had retired to her nest under the windfall a quill had completely pierced his lip and began to prick his tongue.
10084{_}2830{_}In desperation Kazan chewed viciously upon a piece of wood.
10084{_}2831{_}This broke and crumpled the quill, and destroyed its power to do further harm.
10084{_}2832{_}Nature had told him the one thing to do to save himself.
10084{_}2833{_}Most of that day he spent in gnawing at wood and crunching mouthfuls of earth and mold between his jaws.
10084{_}2834{_}In this way the barb-toothed points of the quills were dulled and broken as they came through.
10084{_}2835{_}At dusk he crawled under the windfall, and Gray Wolf gently licked his muzzle with her soft cool tongue.
10084{_}2836{_}Frequently during the night Kazan went to the creek and found relief in its ice-cold water.
10084{_}2837{_}The next day he had what the forest people call "porcupine mumps."
10084{_}2838{_}His face was swollen until Gray Wolf would have laughed if she had been human, and not blind.
10084{_}2839{_}His chops bulged like cushions.
10084{_}2840{_}His eyes were mere slits.
10084{_}2841{_}When he went out into the day he blinked, for he could see scarcely better than his sightless mate.
10084{_}2842{_}But the pain was mostly gone.
10084{_}2843{_}The night that followed he began to think of hunting, and the next morning before it was yet dawn he brought a rabbit into their den.
10084{_}2844{_}A few hours later he would have brought a spruce partridge to Gray Wolf, but just as he was about to spring upon his feathered prey the soft chatter of a porcupine a few yards away brought him to a sudden stop.
10084{_}2845{_}Few things could make Kazan drop his tail.
10084{_}2846{_}But that inane and incoherent prattle of the little spiked beast sent him off at double-quick with his tail between his legs.
10084{_}2847{_}As man abhors and evades the creeping serpent, so Kazan would hereafter evade this little creature of the forests that never in animal history has been known to lose its good-humor or pick a quarrel.
10084{_}2848{_}Two weeks of lengthening days, of increasing warmth, of sunshine and hunting, followed Kazan's adventure with the porcupine.
10084{_}2849{_}The last of the snow went rapidly.
10084{_}2850{_}Out of the earth began to spring tips of green.
10084{_}2851{_}The _bakneesh_ vine glistened redder each day, the poplar buds began to split, and in the sunniest spots, between the rocks of the ridges the little white snow-flowers began to give a final proof that spring had come.
10084{_}2852{_}For the first of those two weeks Gray Wolf hunted frequently with Kazan.
10084{_}2853{_}They did not go far.
10084{_}2854{_}The swamp was alive with small game and each day or night they killed fresh meat.
10084{_}2855{_}After the first week Gray Wolf hunted less.
10084{_}2856{_}Then came the soft and balmy night, glorious in the radiance of a full spring moon when she refused to leave the windfall.
10084{_}2857{_}Kazan did not urge her.
10084{_}2858{_}Instinct made him understand, and he did not go far from the windfall that night in his hunt.
10084{_}2859{_}When he returned he brought a rabbit.
10084{_}2860{_}Came then the night when from the darkest corner of the windfall Gray Wolf warned him back with a low snarl.
10084{_}2861{_}He stood in the opening, a rabbit between his jaws.
10084{_}2862{_}He took no offense at the snarl, but stood for a moment, gazing into the gloom where Gray Wolf had hidden herself.
10084{_}2863{_}Then he dropped the rabbit and lay down squarely in the opening.
10084{_}2864{_}After a little he rose restlessly and went outside.
10084{_}2865{_}But he did not leave the windfall.
10084{_}2866{_}It was day when he reentered.
10084{_}2867{_}He sniffed, as he had sniffed once before a long time ago, between the boulders at the top of the Sun Rock.
10084{_}2868{_}That which was in the air was no longer a mystery to him.
10084{_}2869{_}He came nearer and Gray Wolf did not snarl.
10084{_}2870{_}She whined coaxingly as he touched her.
10084{_}2871{_}Then his muzzle found something else.
10084{_}2872{_}It was soft and warm and made a queer little sniffling sound.
10084{_}2873{_}There was a responsive whine in his throat, and in the darkness came the quick soft caress of Gray Wolf's tongue.
10084{_}2874{_}Kazan returned to the sunshine and stretched himself out before the door of the windfall.
10084{_}2875{_}His jaws dropped open, for he was filled with a strange contentment.
10084{_}2876{_}CHAPTER XVIII  THE EDUCATION OF BA-REE   Robbed once of the joys of parenthood by the murder on the Sun Rock, both Gray Wolf and Kazan were different from what they would have been had the big gray lynx not come into their lives at that time.
10084{_}2877{_}As if it were but yesterday they remembered the moonlit night when the lynx brought blindness to Gray Wolf and destroyed her young, and when Kazan had avenged himself and his mate in his terrible fight to the death with their enemy.
10084{_}2878{_}And now, with that soft little handful of life snuggling close up against her, Gray Wolf saw through her blind eyes the tragic picture of that night more vividly than ever and she quivered at every sound, ready to leap in the face of an unseen foe, to rend all flesh that was not the flesh of Kazan.
10084{_}2879{_}And ceaselessly, the slightest sound bringing him to his feet, Kazan watched and guarded.
10084{_}2880{_}He mistrusted the moving shadows.
10084{_}2881{_}The snapping of a twig drew back his upper lip.
10084{_}2882{_}His fangs gleamed menacingly when the soft air brought a strange scent.
10084{_}2883{_}In him, too, the memory of the Sun Rock, the death of their first young and the blinding of Gray Wolf, had given birth to a new instinct.
10084{_}2884{_}Not for an instant was he off his guard.
10084{_}2885{_}As surely as one expects the sun to rise so did he expect that sooner or later their deadly enemy would creep on them from out of the forest.
10084{_}2886{_}In another hour such as this the lynx had brought death.
10084{_}2887{_}The lynx had brought blindness.
10084{_}2888{_}And so day and night he waited and watched for the lynx to come again.
10084{_}2889{_}And woe unto any other creature of flesh and blood that dared approach the windfall in these first days of Gray Wolf's motherhood!
10084{_}2890{_}But peace had spread its wings of sunshine and plenty over the swamp.
10084{_}2891{_}There were no intruders, unless the noisy whisky-jacks, the big-eyed moose-birds, the chattering bush sparrows, and the wood-mice and ermine could be called such.
10084{_}2892{_}After the first day or two Kazan went more frequently into the windfall, and though more than once he nosed searchingly about Gray Wolf he could find only the one little pup.
10084{_}2893{_}A little farther west the Dog-Ribs would have called the pup Ba-ree for two reasons--because he had no brothers or sisters, and because he was a mixture of dog and wolf.
10084{_}2894{_}He was a sleek and lively little fellow from the beginning, for there was no division of mother strength and attention.
10084{_}2895{_}He developed with the true swiftness of the wolf-whelp, and not with the slowness of the dog-pup.
10084{_}2896{_}For three days he was satisfied to cuddle close against his mother, feeding when he was hungry, sleeping a great deal and preened and laundered almost constantly by Gray Wolf's affectionate tongue.
10084{_}2897{_}From the fourth day he grew busier and more inquisitive with every hour.
10084{_}2898{_}He found his mother's blind face, with tremendous effort he tumbled over her paws, and once he lost himself completely and sniffled for help when he rolled fifteen or eighteen inches away from her.
10084{_}2899{_}It was not long after this that he began to recognize Kazan as a part of his mother, and he was scarcely more than a week old when he rolled himself up contentedly between Kazan's forelegs and went to sleep.
10084{_}2900{_}Kazan was puzzled.
10084{_}2901{_}Then with a deep sigh Gray Wolf laid her head across one of her mate's forelegs, with her nose touching her runaway baby, and seemed vastly contented.
10084{_}2902{_}For half an hour Kazan did not move.
10084{_}2903{_}When he was ten days old Ba-ree discovered there was great sport in tussling with a bit of rabbit fur.
10084{_}2904{_}It was a little later when he made his second exciting discovery--light and sunshine.
10084{_}2905{_}The sun had now reached a point where in the middle of the afternoon a bright gleam of it found its way through an overhead opening in the windfall.
10084{_}2906{_}At first Ba-ree would only stare at the golden streak.
10084{_}2907{_}Then came the time when he tried to play with it as he played with the rabbit fur.
10084{_}2908{_}Each day thereafter he went a little nearer the opening through which Kazan passed from the windfall into the big world outside.
10084{_}2909{_}Finally came the time when he reached the opening and crouched there, blinking and frightened at what he saw, and now Gray Wolf no longer tried to hold him back but went out into the sunshine and tried to call him to her.
10084{_}2910{_}It was three days before his weak eyes had grown strong enough to permit his following her, and very quickly after that Ba-ree learned to love the sun, the warm air, and the sweetness of life, and to dread the darkness of the closed-in den where he had been born.
10084{_}2911{_}That this world was not altogether so nice as it at first appeared he was very soon to learn.
10084{_}2912{_}At the darkening signs of an approaching storm one day Gray Wolf tried to lure him back under the windfall.
10084{_}2913{_}It was her first warning to Ba-ree and he did not understand.
10084{_}2914{_}Where Gray Wolf failed, nature came to teach a first lesson.
10084{_}2915{_}Ba-ree was caught in a sudden deluge of rain.
10084{_}2916{_}It flattened him out in pure terror and he was drenched and half drowned before Gray Wolf caught him between her jaws and carried him into shelter.
10084{_}2917{_}One by one after this the first strange experiences of life came to him, and one by one his instincts received their birth.
10084{_}2918{_}Greatest for him of the days to follow was that on which his inquisitive nose touched the raw flesh of a freshly killed and bleeding rabbit.
10084{_}2919{_}It was his first taste of blood.
10084{_}2920{_}It was sweet.
10084{_}2921{_}It filled him with a strange excitement and thereafter he knew what it meant when Kazan brought in something between his jaws.
10084{_}2922{_}He soon began to battle with sticks in place of the soft fur and his teeth grew as hard and as sharp as little needles.
10084{_}2923{_}The Great Mystery was bared to him at last when Kazan brought in between his jaws, a big rabbit that was still alive but so badly crushed that it could not run when dropped to the ground.
10084{_}2924{_}Ba-ree had learned to know what rabbits and partridges meant--the sweet warm blood that he loved better even than he had ever loved his mother's milk.
10084{_}2925{_}But they had come to him dead.
10084{_}2926{_}He had never seen one of the monsters alive.
10084{_}2927{_}And now the rabbit that Kazan dropped to the ground, kicking and struggling with a broken back, sent Ba-ree back appalled.
10084{_}2928{_}For a few moments he wonderingly watched the dying throes of Kazan's prey.
10084{_}2929{_}Both Kazan and Gray Wolf seemed to understand that this was to be Ba-ree's first lesson in his education as a slaying and flesh-eating creature, and they stood close over the rabbit, making no effort to end its struggles.
10084{_}2930{_}Half a dozen times Gray Wolf sniffed at the rabbit and then turned her blind face toward Ba-ree.
10084{_}2931{_}After the third or fourth time Kazan stretched himself out on his belly a few feet away and watched the proceedings attentively.
10084{_}2932{_}Each time that Gray Wolf lowered her head to muzzle the rabbit Ba-ree's little ears shot up expectantly.
10084{_}2933{_}When he saw that nothing happened and that his mother was not hurt he came a little nearer.
10084{_}2934{_}Soon he could reach out, stiff-legged and cautious, and touch the furry thing that was not yet dead.
10084{_}2935{_}In a last spasmodic convulsion the big rabbit doubled up its rear legs and gave a kick that sent Ba-ree sprawling back, yelping in terror.
10084{_}2936{_}He regained his feet and then, for the first time, anger and the desire to retaliate took possession of him.
10084{_}2937{_}The kick had completed his first education.
10084{_}2938{_}He came back with less caution, but stiffer-legged, and a moment later had dug his tiny teeth in the rabbit's neck.
10084{_}2939{_}He could feel the throb of life in the soft body, the muscles of the dying rabbit twitched convulsively under him, and he hung with his teeth until there was no longer a tremor of life in his first kill.
10084{_}2940{_}Gray Wolf was delighted.
10084{_}2941{_}She caressed Ba-ree with her tongue, and even Kazan condescended to sniff approvingly of his son when he returned to the rabbit.
10084{_}2942{_}And never before had warm sweet blood tasted so good to Ba-ree as it did to-day.
10084{_}2943{_}Swiftly Ba-ree developed from a blood-tasting into a flesh-eating animal.
10084{_}2944{_}One by one the mysteries of life were unfolded to him--the mating-night chortle of the gray owl, the crash of a falling tree, the roll of thunder, the rush of running water, the scream of a fisher-cat, the mooing of the cow moose, and the distant call of his tribe.
10084{_}2945{_}But chief of all these mysteries that were already becoming a part of his instinct was the mystery of scent.
10084{_}2946{_}One day he wandered fifty yards away from the windfall and his little nose touched the warm scent of a rabbit.
10084{_}2947{_}Instantly, without reasoning or further process of education, he knew that to get at the sweet flesh and blood which he loved he must follow the scent.
10084{_}2948{_}He wriggled slowly along the trail until he came to a big log, over which the rabbit had vaulted in a long leap, and from this log he turned back.
10084{_}2949{_}Each day after this he went on adventures of his own.
10084{_}2950{_}At first he was like an explorer without a compass in a vast and unknown world.
10084{_}2951{_}Each day he encountered something new, always wonderful, frequently terrifying.
10084{_}2952{_}But his terrors grew less and less and his confidence correspondingly greater.
10084{_}2953{_}As he found that none of the things he feared did him any harm he became more and more bold in his investigations.
10084{_}2954{_}And his appearance was changing, as well as his view of things.
10084{_}2955{_}His round roly-poly body was taking a different form.
10084{_}2956{_}He became lithe and quick.
10084{_}2957{_}The yellow of his coat darkened, and there was a whitish-gray streak along his back like that along Kazan's.
10084{_}2958{_}He had his mother's under-throat and her beautiful grace of head.
10084{_}2959{_}Otherwise he was a true son of Kazan.
10084{_}2960{_}His limbs gave signs of future strength and massiveness.
10084{_}2961{_}He was broad across the chest.
10084{_}2962{_}His eyes were wide apart, with a little red in the lower corners.
10084{_}2963{_}The forest people know what to expect of husky pups who early develop that drop of red.
10084{_}2964{_}It is a warning that they are born of the wild and that their mothers, or fathers, are of the savage hunt-packs.
10084{_}2965{_}In Ba-ree that tinge of red was so pronounced that it could mean but one thing.
10084{_}2966{_}While he was almost half dog, the wild had claimed him forever.
10084{_}2967{_}Not until the day of his first real battle with a living creature did Ba-ree come fully into his inheritance.
10084{_}2968{_}He had gone farther than usual from the windfall--fully a hundred yards.
10084{_}2969{_}Here he found a new wonder.
10084{_}2970{_}It was the creek.
10084{_}2971{_}He had heard it before and he had looked down on it from afar--from a distance of fifty yards at least.
10084{_}2972{_}But to-day he ventured going to the edge of it, and there he stood for a long time, with the water rippling and singing at his feet, gazing across it into the new world that he saw.
10084{_}2973{_}Then he moved cautiously along the stream.
10084{_}2974{_}He had not gone a dozen steps when there was a furious fluttering close to him, and one of the fierce big-eyed jays of the Northland was directly in his path.
10084{_}2975{_}It could not fly.
10084{_}2976{_}One of its wings dragged, probably broken in a struggle with some one of the smaller preying beasts.
10084{_}2977{_}But for an instant it was a most startling and defiant bit of life to Ba-ree.
10084{_}2978{_}Then the grayish crest along his back stiffened and he advanced.
10084{_}2979{_}The wounded jay remained motionless until Ba-ree was within three feet of it.
10084{_}2980{_}In short quick hops it began to retreat.
10084{_}2981{_}Instantly Ba-ree's indecision had flown to the four winds.
10084{_}2982{_}With one sharp excited yelp he flew at the defiant bird.
10084{_}2983{_}For a few moments there was a thrilling race, and Ba-ree's sharp little teeth buried themselves in the jay's feathers.
10084{_}2984{_}Swift as a flash the bird's beak began to strike.
10084{_}2985{_}The jay was the king of the smaller birds.
10084{_}2986{_}In nesting season it killed the brush sparrows, the mild-eyed moose-birds, and the tree-sappers.
10084{_}2987{_}Again and again it struck Ba-ree with its powerful beak, but the son of Kazan had now reached the age of battle and the pain of the blows only made his own teeth sink deeper.
10084{_}2988{_}At last he found the flesh; and a puppyish snarl rose in his throat.
10084{_}2989{_}Fortunately he had gained a hold under the wing and after the first dozen blows the jay's resistance grew weaker.
10084{_}2990{_}Five minutes later Ba-ree loosened his teeth and drew back a step to look at the crumpled and motionless creature before him.
10084{_}2991{_}The jay was dead.
10084{_}2992{_}He had won his first battle.
10084{_}2993{_}And with victory came the wonderful dawning of that greatest instinct of all, which told him that no longer was he a drone in the marvelous mechanism of wilderness life--but a part of it from this time forth.
10084{_}2994{_}_For he had killed_.
10084{_}2995{_}Half an hour later Gray Wolf came down over his trail.
10084{_}2996{_}The jay was torn into bits.
10084{_}2997{_}Its feathers were scattered about and Ba-ree's little nose was bloody.
10084{_}2998{_}Ba-ree was lying in triumph beside his victim.
10084{_}2999{_}Swiftly Gray Wolf understood and caressed him joyously.
10084{_}3000{_}When they returned to the windfall Ba-ree carried in his jaws what was left of the jay.
10084{_}3001{_}From that hour of his first kill hunting became the chief passion of Ba-ree's life.
10084{_}3002{_}When he was not sleeping in the sun, or under the windfall at night, he was seeking life that he could destroy.
10084{_}3003{_}He slaughtered an entire family of wood-mice.
10084{_}3004{_}Moose-birds were at first the easiest for him to stalk, and he killed three.
10084{_}3005{_}Then he encountered an ermine and the fierce little white outlaw of the forests gave him his first defeat.
10084{_}3006{_}Defeat cooled his ardor for a few days, but taught him the great lesson that there were other fanged and flesh-eating animals besides himself and that nature had so schemed things that fang must not prey upon fang--_for food_.
10084{_}3007{_}Many things had been born in him.
10084{_}3008{_}Instinctively he shunned the porcupine without experiencing the torture of its quills.
10084{_}3009{_}He came face to face with a fisher-cat one day, a fortnight after his fight with the ermine.
10084{_}3010{_}Both were seeking food, and as there was no food between them to fight over, each went his own way.
10084{_}3011{_}Farther and farther Ba-ree ventured from the windfall, always following the creek.
10084{_}3012{_}Sometimes he was gone for hours.
10084{_}3013{_}At first Gray Wolf was restless when he was away, but she seldom went with him and after a time her restlessness left her.
10084{_}3014{_}Nature was working swiftly.
10084{_}3015{_}It was Kazan who was restless now.
10084{_}3016{_}Moonlight nights had come and the wanderlust was growing more and more insistent in his veins.
10084{_}3017{_}And Gray Wolf, too, was filled with the strange longing to roam at large out into the big world.
10084{_}3018{_}Came then the afternoon when Ba-ree went on his longest hunt.
10084{_}3019{_}Half a mile away he killed his first rabbit.
10084{_}3020{_}He remained beside it until dusk.
10084{_}3021{_}The moon rose, big and golden, flooding the forests and plains and ridges with a light almost like that of day.
10084{_}3022{_}It was a glorious night.
10084{_}3023{_}And Ba-ree found the moon, and left his kill.
10084{_}3024{_}And the direction in which he traveled _was away from the windfall_.
10084{_}3025{_}All that night Gray Wolf watched and waited.
10084{_}3026{_}And when at last the moon was sinking into the south and west she settled back on her haunches, turned her blind face to the sky and sent forth her first howl since the day Ba-ree was born.
10084{_}3027{_}Nature had come into her own.
10084{_}3028{_}Far away Ba-ree heard, but he did not answer.
10084{_}3029{_}A new world was his.
10084{_}3030{_}He had said good-by to the windfall--and home.
10084{_}3031{_}CHAPTER XIX  THE USURPERS   It was that glorious season between spring and summer, when the northern nights were brilliant with moon and stars, that Kazan and Gray Wolf set up the valley between the two ridges on a long hunt.
10084{_}3032{_}It was the beginning of that _wanderlust_ which always comes to the furred and padded creatures of the wilderness immediately after the young-born of early spring have left their mothers to find their own way in the big world.
10084{_}3033{_}They struck west from their winter home under the windfall in the swamp.
10084{_}3034{_}They hunted mostly at night and behind them they left a trail marked by the partly eaten carcasses of rabbits and partridges.
10084{_}3035{_}It was the season of slaughter and not of hunger.
10084{_}3036{_}Ten miles west of the swamp they killed a fawn.
10084{_}3037{_}This, too, they left after a single meal.
10084{_}3038{_}Their appetites became satiated with warm flesh and blood.
10084{_}3039{_}They grew sleek and fat and each day they basked longer in the warm sunshine.
10084{_}3040{_}They had few rivals.
10084{_}3041{_}The lynxes were in the heavier timber to the south.
10084{_}3042{_}There were no wolves.
10084{_}3043{_}Fisher-cat, marten and mink were numerous along the creek, but these were neither swift-hunting nor long-fanged.
10084{_}3044{_}One day they came upon an old otter.
10084{_}3045{_}He was a giant of his kind, turning a whitish gray with the approach of summer.
10084{_}3046{_}Kazan, grown fat and lazy, watched him idly.
10084{_}3047{_}Blind Gray Wolf sniffed at the fishy smell of him in the air.
10084{_}3048{_}To them he was no more than a floating stick, a creature out of their element, along with the fish, and they continued on their way not knowing that this uncanny creature with the coal-like flappers was soon to become their ally in one of the strange and deadly feuds of the wilderness, which are as sanguinary to animal life as the deadliest feuds of men are to human life.
10084{_}3049{_}The day following their meeting with the otter Gray Wolf and Kazan continued three miles farther westward, still following the stream.
10084{_}3050{_}Here they encountered the interruption to their progress which turned them over the northward ridge.
10084{_}3051{_}The obstacle was a huge beaver dam.
10084{_}3052{_}The dam was two hundred yards in width and flooded a mile of swamp and timber above it.
10084{_}3053{_}Neither Gray Wolf nor Kazan was deeply interested in beavers.
10084{_}3054{_}They also moved out of their element, along with the fish and the otter and swift-winged birds.
10084{_}3055{_}So they turned into the north, not knowing that nature had already schemed that they four--the dog, wolf, otter and beaver--should soon be engaged in one of those merciless struggles of the wild which keep animal life down to the survival of the fittest, and whose tragic histories are kept secret under the stars and the moon and the winds that tell no tales.
10084{_}3056{_}For many years no man had come into this valley between the two ridges to molest the beaver.
10084{_}3057{_}If a Sarcee trapper had followed down the nameless creek and had caught the patriarch and chief of the colony, he would at once have judged him to be very old and his Indian tongue would have given him a name.
10084{_}3058{_}He would have called him Broken Tooth, because one of the four long teeth with which he felled trees and built dams was broken off.
10084{_}3059{_}Six years before Broken Tooth had led a few beavers of his own age down the stream, and they had built their first small dam and their first lodge.
10084{_}3060{_}The following April Broken Tooth's mate had four little baby beavers, and each of the other mothers in the colony increased the population by two or three or four.
10084{_}3061{_}At the end of the fourth year this first generation of children, had they followed the usual law of nature, would have mated and left the colony to build a dam and lodges of their own.
10084{_}3062{_}They mated, but did not emigrate.
10084{_}3063{_}The next year the second generation of children, now four years old, mated but did not leave, so that in this early summer of the sixth year the colony was very much like a great city that had been long besieged by an enemy.
10084{_}3064{_}It numbered fifteen lodges and over a hundred beavers, not counting the fourth babies which had been born during March and April.
10084{_}3065{_}The dam had been lengthened until it was fully two hundred yards in length.
10084{_}3066{_}Water had been made to flood large areas of birch and poplar and tangled swamps of tender willow and elder.
10084{_}3067{_}Even with this food was growing scarce and the lodges were overcrowded.
10084{_}3068{_}This was because beavers are almost human in their love for home.
10084{_}3069{_}Broken Tooth's lodge was fully nine feet long by seven wide inside, and there were now living in it children and grandchildren to the number of twenty-seven.
10084{_}3070{_}For this reason Broken Tooth was preparing to break the precedent of his tribe.
10084{_}3071{_}When Kazan and Gray Wolf sniffed carelessly at the strong scents of the beaver city, Broken Tooth was marshaling his family, and two of his sons and their families, for the exodus.
10084{_}3072{_}As yet Broken Tooth was the recognized leader in the colony.
10084{_}3073{_}No other beaver had grown to his size and strength.
10084{_}3074{_}His thick body was fully three feet long.
10084{_}3075{_}He weighed at least sixty pounds.
10084{_}3076{_}His tail was fourteen inches in length and five in width, and on a still night he could strike the water a blow that could be heard a quarter of a mile away.
10084{_}3077{_}His webbed hindfeet were twice as large as his mate's and he was easily the swiftest swimmer in the colony.
10084{_}3078{_}Following the afternoon when Gray Wolf and Kazan struck into the north came the clear still night when Broken Tooth climbed to the top of the dam, shook himself, and looked down to see that his army was behind him.
10084{_}3079{_}The starlit water of the big pond rippled and flashed with the movement of many bodies.
10084{_}3080{_}A few of the older beavers clambered up after Broken Tooth and the old patriarch plunged down into the narrow stream on the other side of the dam.
10084{_}3081{_}Now the shining silken bodies of the emigrants followed him in the starlight.
10084{_}3082{_}In ones and twos and threes they climbed over the dam and with them went a dozen children born three months before.
10084{_}3083{_}Easily and swiftly they began the journey down-stream, the youngsters swimming furiously to keep up with their parents.
10084{_}3084{_}In all they numbered forty.
10084{_}3085{_}Broken Tooth swam well in the lead, with his older workers and battlers behind him.
10084{_}3086{_}In the rear followed mothers and children.
10084{_}3087{_}All of that night the journey continued.
10084{_}3088{_}The otter, their deadliest enemy--deadlier even than man--hid himself in a thick clump of willows as they passed.
10084{_}3089{_}Nature, which sometimes sees beyond the vision of man, had made him the enemy of these creatures that were passing his hiding-place in the night.
10084{_}3090{_}A fish-feeder, he was born to be a conserver as well as a destroyer of the creatures on which he fed.
10084{_}3091{_}Perhaps nature told him that too many beaver dams stopped the run of spawning fish and that where there were many beavers there were always few fish.
10084{_}3092{_}Maybe he reasoned as to why fish-hunting was poor and he went hungry.
10084{_}3093{_}So, unable to cope singly with whole tribes of his enemies, he worked to destroy their dams.
10084{_}3094{_}How this, in turn, destroyed the beavers will be seen in the feud in which nature had already schemed that he should play a part with Kazan and Gray Wolf.
10084{_}3095{_}A dozen times during this night Broken Tooth halted to investigate the food supplies along the banks.
10084{_}3096{_}But in the two or three places where he found plenty of the bark on which they lived it would have been difficult to have constructed a dam.
10084{_}3097{_}His wonderful engineering instincts rose even above food instincts.
10084{_}3098{_}And when each time he moved onward, no beaver questioned his judgment by remaining behind.
10084{_}3099{_}In the early dawn they crossed the burn and came to the edge of the swamp domain of Kazan and Gray Wolf.
10084{_}3100{_}By right of discovery and possession that swamp belonged to the dog and the wolf.
10084{_}3101{_}In every part of it they had left their mark of ownership.
10084{_}3102{_}But Broken Tooth was a creature of the water and the scent of his tribe was not keen.
10084{_}3103{_}He led on, traveling more slowly when they entered the timber.
10084{_}3104{_}Just below the windfall home of Kazan and Gray Wolf he halted, and clambering ashore balanced himself upright on his webbed hindfeet and broad four-pound tail.
10084{_}3105{_}Here he had found ideal conditions.
10084{_}3106{_}A dam could be constructed easily across the narrow stream, and the water could be made to flood a big supply of poplar, birch, willow and alder.
10084{_}3107{_}Also the place was sheltered by heavy timber, so that the winters would be warm.
10084{_}3108{_}Broken Tooth quickly gave his followers to understand that this was to be their new home.
10084{_}3109{_}On both sides of the stream they swarmed into the near-by timber.
10084{_}3110{_}The babies began at once to nibble hungrily at the tender bark of willow and alder.
10084{_}3111{_}The older ones, every one of them now a working engineer, investigated excitedly, breakfasting by nibbling off a mouthful of bark now and then.
10084{_}3112{_}That day the work of home-building began.
10084{_}3113{_}Broken Tooth himself selected a big birch that leaned over the stream, and began the work of cutting through the ten-inch butt with his three long teeth.
10084{_}3114{_}Though the old patriarch had lost one tooth, the three that remained had not deteriorated with age.
10084{_}3115{_}The outer edge of them was formed of the hardest enamel; the inner side was of soft ivory.
10084{_}3116{_}They were like the finest steel chisels, the enamel never wearing away and the softer ivory replacing itself year by year as it was consumed.
10084{_}3117{_}Sitting on his hindlegs, with his forepaws resting against the tree and with his heavy tail giving him a firm balance, Broken Tooth began gnawing a narrow ring entirely around the tree.
10084{_}3118{_}He worked tirelessly for several hours, and when at last he stopped to rest another workman took up the task.
10084{_}3119{_}Meanwhile a dozen beavers were hard at work cutting timber.
10084{_}3120{_}Long before Broken Tooth's tree was ready to fall across the stream, a smaller poplar crashed into the water.
10084{_}3121{_}The cutting on the big birch was in the shape of an hour-glass.
10084{_}3122{_}In twenty hours it fell straight across the creek.
10084{_}3123{_}While the beaver prefers to do most of his work at night he is a day-laborer as well, and Broken Tooth gave his tribe but little rest during the days that followed.
10084{_}3124{_}With almost human intelligence the little engineers kept at their task.
10084{_}3125{_}Smaller trees were felled, and these were cut into four or five foot lengths.
10084{_}3126{_}One by one these lengths were rolled to the stream, the beavers pushing them with their heads and forepaws, and by means of brush and small limbs they were fastened securely against the birch.
10084{_}3127{_}When the framework was completed the wonderful cement construction was begun.
10084{_}3128{_}In this the beavers were the masters of men.
10084{_}3129{_}Dynamite was the only force that could hereafter break up what they were building now.
10084{_}3130{_}Under their cup-like chins the beavers brought from the banks a mixture of mud and fine twigs, carrying from half a pound to a pound at a load and began filling up the framework with it.
10084{_}3131{_}Their task seemed tremendous, and yet Broken Tooth's engineers could carry a ton of this mud and twig mixture during a day and night.
10084{_}3132{_}In three days the water was beginning to back, until it rose about the butts of a dozen or more trees and was flooding a small area of brush.
10084{_}3133{_}This made work easier.
10084{_}3134{_}From now on materials could be cut in the water and easily floated.
10084{_}3135{_}While a part of the beaver colony was taking advantage of the water, others were felling trees end to end with the birch, laying the working frame of a dam a hundred feet in width.
10084{_}3136{_}They had nearly accomplished this work when one morning Kazan and Gray Wolf returned to the swamp.
10084{_}3137{_}CHAPTER XX  A FEUD IN THE WILDERNESS   A soft wind blowing from the south and east brought the scent of the invaders to Gray Wolf's nose when they were still half a mile away.
10084{_}3138{_}She gave the warning to Kazan and he, too, found the strange scent in the air.
10084{_}3139{_}It grew stronger as they advanced.
10084{_}3140{_}When two hundred yards from the windfall they heard the sudden crash of a falling tree, and stopped.
10084{_}3141{_}For a full minute they stood tense and listening.
10084{_}3142{_}Then the silence was broken by a squeaking cry, followed by a splash.
10084{_}3143{_}Gray Wolf's alert ears fell back and she turned her blind face understandingly toward Kazan.
10084{_}3144{_}They trotted ahead slowly, approaching the windfall from behind.
10084{_}3145{_}Not until they had reached the top of the knoll on which it was situated did Kazan begin to see the wonderful change that had taken place during their absence.
10084{_}3146{_}Astounded, they stood while he stared.
10084{_}3147{_}There was no longer a little creek below them.
10084{_}3148{_}Where it had been was a pond that reached almost to the foot of the knoll.
10084{_}3149{_}It was fully a hundred feet in width and the backwater had flooded the trees and bush for five or six times that distance toward the burn.
10084{_}3150{_}They had come up quietly and Broken Tooth's dull-scented workers were unaware of their presence.
10084{_}3151{_}Not fifty feet away Broken Tooth himself was gnawing at the butt of a tree.
10084{_}3152{_}An equal distance to the right of him four or five of the baby beavers were at play building a miniature dam of mud and tiny twigs.
10084{_}3153{_}On the opposite side of the pond was a steep bank six or seven feet high, and here a few of the older children--two years old, but still not workmen--were having great fun climbing the bank and using it as a toboggan-slide.
10084{_}3154{_}It was their splashing that Kazan and Gray Wolf had heard.
10084{_}3155{_}In a dozen different places the older beavers were at work.
10084{_}3156{_}A few weeks before Kazan had looked upon a similar scene when he had returned into the north from Broken Tooth's old home.
10084{_}3157{_}It had not interested him then.
10084{_}3158{_}But a quick and thrilling change swept through him now.
10084{_}3159{_}The beavers had ceased to be mere water animals, uneatable and with an odor that displeased him.
10084{_}3160{_}They were invaders--and enemies.
10084{_}3161{_}His fangs bared silently.
10084{_}3162{_}His crest stiffened like the hair of a brush, and the muscles of his forelegs and shoulders stood out like whipcords.
10084{_}3163{_}Not a sound came from him as he rushed down upon Broken Tooth.
10084{_}3164{_}The old beaver was oblivious of danger until Kazan was within twenty feet of him.
10084{_}3165{_}Naturally slow of movement on land, he stood for an instant stupefied.
10084{_}3166{_}Then he swung down from the tree as Kazan leaped upon him.
10084{_}3167{_}Over and over they rolled to the edge of the bank, carried on by the dog's momentum.
10084{_}3168{_}In another moment the thick heavy body of the beaver had slipped like oil from under Kazan and Broken Tooth was safe in his element, two holes bitten clean through his fleshy tail.
10084{_}3169{_}Baffled in his effort to get a death-hold on Broken Tooth, Kazan swung like a flash to the right.
10084{_}3170{_}The young beavers had not moved.
10084{_}3171{_}Astonished and frightened at what they had seen, they stood as if stupefied.
10084{_}3172{_}Not until they saw Kazan tearing toward them did they awaken to action.
10084{_}3173{_}Three of them reached the water.
10084{_}3174{_}The fourth and fifth--baby beavers not more than three months old--were too late.
10084{_}3175{_}With a single snap of his jaw Kazan broke the hack of one.
10084{_}3176{_}The other he pinned down by the throat and shook as a terrier shakes a rat.
10084{_}3177{_}When Gray Wolf trotted down to him both of the little beavers were dead.
10084{_}3178{_}She sniffed at their soft little bodies and whined.
10084{_}3179{_}Perhaps the baby creatures reminded her of runaway Ba-ree, her own baby, for there was a note of longing in her whine as she nosed them.
10084{_}3180{_}It was the mother whine.
10084{_}3181{_}But if Gray Wolf had visions of her own Kazan understood nothing of them.
10084{_}3182{_}He had killed two of the creatures that had dared to invade their home.
10084{_}3183{_}To the little beavers he had been as merciless as the gray lynx that had murdered Gray Wolf's first children on the top of the Sun Rock.
10084{_}3184{_}Now that he had sunk his teeth into the flesh of his enemies his blood was filled with a frenzied desire to kill.
10084{_}3185{_}He raved along the edge of the pond, snarling at the uneasy water under which Broken Tooth had disappeared.
10084{_}3186{_}All of the beavers had taken refuge in the pond, and its surface was heaving with the passing of many bodies beneath.
10084{_}3187{_}Kazan came to the end of the dam.
10084{_}3188{_}This was new.
10084{_}3189{_}Instinctively he knew that it was the work of Broken Tooth and his tribe and for a few moments he tore fiercely at the matted sticks and limbs.
10084{_}3190{_}Suddenly there was an upheaval of water close to the dam, fifty feet out from the bank, and Broken Tooth's big gray head appeared.
10084{_}3191{_}For a tense half minute Broken Tooth and Kazan measured each other at that distance.
10084{_}3192{_}Then Broken Tooth drew his wet shining body out of the water to the top of the dam, and squatted flat, facing Kazan.
10084{_}3193{_}The old patriarch was alone.
10084{_}3194{_}Not another beaver had shown himself.
10084{_}3195{_}The surface of the pond had now become quiet.
10084{_}3196{_}Vainly Kazan tried to discover a footing that would allow him to reach the watchful invader.
10084{_}3197{_}But between the solid wall of the dam and the bank there was a tangled framework through which the water rushed with some violence.
10084{_}3198{_}Three times Kazan fought to work his way through that tangle, and three times his efforts ended in sudden plunges into the water.
10084{_}3199{_}All this time Broken Tooth did not move.
10084{_}3200{_}When at last Kazan gave up the attack the old engineer slipped over the edge of the dam and disappeared under the water.
10084{_}3201{_}He had learned that Kazan, like the lynx, could not fight water and he spread the news among the members of his colony.
10084{_}3202{_}Gray Wolf and Kazan returned to the windfall and lay down in the warm sun.
10084{_}3203{_}Half an hour later Broken Tooth drew himself out on the opposite shore of the pond.
10084{_}3204{_}He was followed by other beavers.
10084{_}3205{_}Across the water they resumed their work as if nothing had happened.
10084{_}3206{_}The tree-cutters returned to their trees.
10084{_}3207{_}Half a dozen worked in the water, carrying loads of cement and twigs.
10084{_}3208{_}The middle of the pond was their dead-line.
10084{_}3209{_}Across this not one of them passed.
10084{_}3210{_}A dozen times during the hour that followed one of the beavers swam up to the dead-line, and rested there, looking at the shining little bodies of the babies that Kazan had killed.
10084{_}3211{_}Perhaps it was the mother, and perhaps some finer instinct unknown to Kazan told this to Gray Wolf.
10084{_}3212{_}For Gray Wolf went down twice to sniff at the dead bodies, and each time--without seeing--she went when the mother beaver had come to the dead-line.
10084{_}3213{_}The first fierce animus had worn itself from Kazan's blood, and he now watched the beavers closely.
10084{_}3214{_}He had learned that they were not fighters.
10084{_}3215{_}They were many to one and yet they ran from him like a lot of rabbits.
10084{_}3216{_}Broken Tooth had not even struck at him, and slowly it grew upon him that these invading creatures that used both the water and land would have to be hunted as he stalked the rabbit and the partridge.
10084{_}3217{_}Early in the afternoon he slipped off into the bush, followed by Gray Wolf.
10084{_}3218{_}He had often begun the stalking of a rabbit by moving _away_ from it and he employed this wolf trick now with the beavers.
10084{_}3219{_}Beyond the windfall he turned and began trotting up the creek, with the wind.
10084{_}3220{_}For a quarter of a mile the creek was deeper than it had ever been.
10084{_}3221{_}One of their old fording places was completely submerged, and at last Kazan plunged in and swam across, leaving Gray Wolf to wait for him on the windfall side of the stream.
10084{_}3222{_}Alone he made his way quickly in the direction of the dam, traveling two hundred yards back from the creek.
10084{_}3223{_}Twenty yards below the dam a dense thicket of alder and willow grew close to the creek and Kazan took advantage of this.
10084{_}3224{_}He approached within a leap or two of the dam without being seen and crouched close to the ground, ready to spring forth when the opportunity came.
10084{_}3225{_}Most of the beavers were now working in the water.
10084{_}3226{_}The four or five still on shore were close to the water and some distance up-stream.
10084{_}3227{_}After a wait of several minutes Kazan was almost on the point of staking everything on a wild rush upon his enemies when a movement on the dam attracted his attention.
10084{_}3228{_}Half-way out two or three beavers were at work strengthening the central structure with cement.
10084{_}3229{_}Swift as a flash Kazan darted from his cover to the shelter behind the dam.
10084{_}3230{_}Here the water was very shallow, the main portion of the stream finding a passage close to the opposite shore.
10084{_}3231{_}Nowhere did it reach to his belly as he waded out.
10084{_}3232{_}He was completely hidden from the beavers, and the wind was in his favor.
10084{_}3233{_}The noise of running water drowned what little sound he made.
10084{_}3234{_}Soon he heard the beaver workmen over him.
10084{_}3235{_}The branches of the fallen birch gave him a footing, and he clambered up.
10084{_}3236{_}A moment later his head and shoulders appeared above the top of the dam.
10084{_}3237{_}Scarce an arm's length away Broken Tooth was forcing into place a three-foot length of poplar as big around as a man's arm.
10084{_}3238{_}He was so busy that he did not hear or see Kazan.
10084{_}3239{_}Another beaver gave the warning as he plunged into the pond.
10084{_}3240{_}Broken Tooth looked up, and his eyes met Kazan's bared fangs.
10084{_}3241{_}There was no time to turn.
10084{_}3242{_}He threw himself back, but it was a moment too late.
10084{_}3243{_}Kazan was upon him.
10084{_}3244{_}His long fangs sank deep into Broken Tooth's neck.
10084{_}3245{_}But the old beaver had thrown himself enough back to make Kazan lose his footing.
10084{_}3246{_}At the same moment his chisel-like teeth got a firm hold of the loose skin at Kazan's throat.
